1601 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Laguna Publishing Co. v. Golden West Publishing Corp.


Civ. No. 20650.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA,FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


110 Cal. App. 3d 43; 167 Cal. Rptr. 687; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 2225; 1980 Trade Cas. (CCH) P63,578



September 4, 1980 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REHEARING


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehg. granted Oct. 2, 1981 (See 124 C.A.3d 967)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. 207112, Walter W. Charamza, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Orange County (California) denying appellant's application for an injunction to terminate appellee's exclusion of appellant's newspaper from appellee's gated community and limiting jury trial issues to violations of the Cartwright Act and Unfair Trade Practices Act.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of an order denying an application for an injunction to terminate appellee community's exclusion of appellant's newspaper from its gated community and limiting jury trial issues to Cartwright Act and Unfair Trade Practices Act. Appellant sought to distribute its unsolicited give-away newspaper to the private residences of appellee's walled and gated private retirement community. Appellee was the corporation who owned the streets, sidewalks and other common property in the retirement community. The other appellee, a competing give-away newspaper, was permitted to deliver its paper to the community because it had by a single agreement subscribed all the private residences to the paper. The court reversed the trial court's denial of appellant's request for injunctive relief finding that, if the appellee community was permitting a competing paper into the community, it must also let appellant's paper in. The court directed the trial court to grant a conditional injunction. The court also directed the trial court to try issues under the California Business and Professions Code subject to the four-year limitation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of appellants request for injunctive relief to terminate appellee's exclusion of appellant's newspaper in appellee's gated community. The court also directed the trial court to try the issues arising from the illegality of the exclusion of appellant's newspaper under the California Business and Professions Code.

 

1602 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


California Teachers Asso. v. Riles


Civ. Nos. 53925, 57263.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA,SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


109 Cal. App. 3d 989; 167 Cal. Rptr. 676; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 2219



September 2, 1980., As modified September 30, 1980


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Hg. granted Dec. 12, 1980 (See 29 C.3d 794)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Nos. C 48751 and C 216450, Ernest J. Zack and Sidney W. Kaufman, Judges.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff teachers association appealed a decision from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which determined that Cal. Educ. Code §§ 60315 and 60246, which allowed the state to lend textbooks to nonprofit schools students, was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff teachers association filed suit to challenge the constitutionality of the statutes which allowed the state to lend textbooks to students who attended non-profit schools in the state. The trial court ruled that the statutes were constitutional. A second suit was filed to challenge the administration of the code provisions. The trial court found the process used to be valid. Plaintiff appealed both decisions. In a consolidated appeal, the court ruled that the statutes, which allowed the loan of obsolete or surplus materials did not violate U.S. Const. amend. I, because it merely made available to all children benefits of a general program. The program had a secular purpose, did not advance religion, and avoided excessive government entanglement with religion. The court also found that the administrative process used to identify and lend the books was constitutionally permissible and it affirmed the decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision which found the statutes which allowed the loan of surplus textbooks to students at nonprofit schools because the program had a secular purpose and avoided excessive government entanglement with religion. It also found the process used to identify and lend the books was constitutionally valid.

 

1603 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Gore v. Board of Medical Quality Assurance


Civ. No. 56996


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


110 Cal. App. 3d 184; 167 Cal. Rptr. 881; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 2238



August 29, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied October 22, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C-232479, Robert I. Weil, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner physician sought review of an order of the Superior Court, Los Angeles County (California), which denied a writ of mandate and upheld an order of respondent medical quality assurance board suspending petitioner's medical license for one year for gross negligence.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner physician's patient died after a hysterectomy. Respondent medical quality assurance board found petitioner grossly negligent and suspended his medical license for one year. The trial court found that one of the board members changed his vote to gross negligence after speaking with several friends outside the proceedings. The trial court issued a peremptory writ of mandate requiring the board to dismiss the accusation or to re-decide the case without the participation of that board member. Respondent made the same finding. The trial court denied petitioner's request for a writ of mandate. The court held that the improper action of the board member during the first hearing did not taint the second hearing. The court held that the judgment of the trial court was supported by substantial evidence because several physicians testified during the administrative hearing that petitioner was grossly negligent in his failure to administer the proper tests. The court held that petitioner was grossly negligent because his management of his patient was an extreme departure from the standard of medical care. Therefore, the court affirmed that judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of petitioner physician's request of writ of mandate requiring respondent medical quality assurance board to reinstate petitioner's medical license because respondent's finding that petitioner was grossly negligent was supported by substantial evidence.

 

1604 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Schuster v. Municipal Court


Civ. No. 22008


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


109 Cal. App. 3d 887; 167 Cal. Rptr. 447; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 2210



August 28, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied September 16, 1980, and the Petition of Real Party in Interest for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 10, 1980. Bird, C. J., was of the Opinion that the Petition should be Granted. The United States Supreme Court Denied a Petition for Writ of Certiorari on April 6, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Imperial County, No. 2249, Donald R. Work, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prosecution sought review of an order of the Superior Court, Imperial County (California) that granted petitioner individuals' request for a writ of prohibition restraining further criminal proceedings against petitioners for alleged violations of Cal. Elec. Code § 29410.


OVERVIEW: Appellant prosecution filed a complaint in respondent municipal court charging petitioner individuals with violating Cal. Elec. Code § 29410. In response, petitioners filed a demurrer to the complaint. Respondent overruled the demurrer, and petitioners sought a writ of prohibition in the superior court. The superior court granted the request for a writ of prohibition and restrained further criminal proceedings against petitioners. Consequently, appellant sought review. On review, the court affirmed the order that granted the writ because Cal. Elec. Code § 29410 was a facially overbroad restraint on the freedom of expression protected by both U.S. Const. amend I and Cal. Const. art. I, § 2.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that granted petitioner individuals' request for a writ of prohibition because the statute petitioners were charged with violating was on its face an unconstitutionally overbroad restraint of the freedom of expression.

 

1605 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Liptak v. Diane Apartments, Inc.


Civ. No. 57654


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


109 Cal. App. 3d 762; 167 Cal. Rptr. 440; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 2199



August 27, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. EAC 29264, Howard D. McClain, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment dismissing the complaint as to Warren in respect to the 17th and 19th causes of action is reversed. The dismissal of the fourth, fifth, and seventh causes of action as to Toups and Warren is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowners sought review of orders of the Superior Court, Los Angeles County (California) that sustained the demurrers of respondent engineers and respondent contractors and granted judgments of dismissal in appellants' action to recover damages to their home caused by earth movement.


OVERVIEW: The house of appellant homeowners was damaged by earth movements. Subsequently, appellants brought suit to recover for such damages against respondent engineers and respondent contractors, among others. Respondents were involved in the grading and filling of the slope that moved and caused the damage. Respondents demurred to the complaint, arguing it was barred on its face by the statute of limitations, Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 337.15. The trial court sustained the demurrers and entered judgments of dismissal. Appellants sought review, contending the 10-year period prescribed by § 337.15 did not commence until the development was substantially completed. On review, the court reversed as to appellants' 17th and 19th causes of action, because the allegations in those causes of action presented a factual dispute over the application of the statute of limitations. However, the court affirmed as to the remainder of the claims against respondents because the alleged defect involved work which was completed more than 10 years prior to the filing of the complaint.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part, affirmed in part, and remanded because the 10-year period provided in the statutes of limitations commenced to run in respect to respondent engineers and respondent contractor at the time their improvements were substantially completed; however, a factual dispute existed under appellant homeowners' 17th and 19th causes of action, regarding the completion date of respondents' activities.

 

1606 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Skelton


Crim. No. 8922


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


109 Cal. App. 3d 691; 167 Cal. Rptr. 636; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 2195



August 26, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitions for a Rehearing were Denied September 11 and September 12, 1980, and Appellants' Petitions for a Hearing by the Supreme Court were Denied October 29, 1980. Mosk, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition of Appellant Curtin should be Granted. The United States Supreme Court Denied Appellant Curtin's Petition for Writ of Certiorari on February 23, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. CR 37345, James L. Focht, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, Skelton's sentence is modified vacating the concurrent sentences as to counts 47 through 51, 57, 68 through 89, 91 through 95, 103, 104 through 116, and 120 through 132, these counts being duplicative of punishment imposed for corresponding theft convictions. In all other respects, Skelton's sentence is affirmed. Similarly, Mack's sentence is modified striking the concurrent sentences as to counts 47 through 54, 56 through 67, 69, 70, 78 through 82, 84 through 89, 91 through 108, 110 through 120, and 122 through 132. As modified, Mack's sentence is affirmed. Curtin's probation untainted by these defects is affirmed. Judgments as modified are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Three defendants appealed their convictions and sentences by the Superior Court, San Diego County (California) for multiple counts of grand theft, Cal. Penal Code § 487, subd. 1; sale of unqualified securities, Cal. Corp. Code § 25110; securities fraud, Cal. Corp. Code §§ 25401 and 25541; and conspiracy to commit grand theft, Cal. Penal Code §§ 182, subd. 1, and 487, subd. 1.


OVERVIEW: Three defendants were convicted of multiple counts of grand theft, Cal. Penal Code § 487, subd. 1; sale of unqualified securities, Cal. Corp. Code § 25110; securities fraud, Cal. Corp. Code §§ 25401 and 25541; and conspiracy to commit grand theft, Cal. Penal Code §§ 182, subd. 1, and 487, subd. 1. The trial court denied their motions for a new trial. Defendants appealed their convictions and sentences, presenting 15 points of error. The appellate court affirmed their convictions, finding no reversible error. However, the court held that the trial court erred when it imposed multiple punishments contrary to the provisions of Cal. Penal Code § 654. The court held that § 654 rendered impermissible the sentences imposed for violation of various sections of the Corporations Code which arose out of the same course of conduct and the same underlying intent to defraud resulting in the theft convictions. The court said that the fact that the sentences were concurrent provided no consolation. The court modified the sentences to comport with its opinion.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendants' convictions for multiple counts of grand theft, sale of unqualified securities, securities fraud, and conspiracy to commit grand theft. However, the court modified defendants' sentences, vacating certain conspiracy counts as duplicative of punishment imposed for corresponding theft convictions.

 

1607 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co. v. Smith


Civ. No. 58386.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA,SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


109 Cal. App. 3d 575; 167 Cal. Rptr. 410; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 2187



August 22, 1980., As modified August 29, 1980


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Hg. granted Oct. 15, 1980 (L.A. 31339).
July 22, 1981, cause retrans. to Ct. of App., 2nd Dist., Div. 1, for reconsideration in light of Farmers insurance Exchange v. Cocking, 29 C.3d 383.
Opn. filed Nov. 20, 1981, not for publication.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. NCC 12194-B, Robert P. Schifferman, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant wife appealed the judgment of the Superior Court, Los Angeles County (California) in declaratory relief in favor of plaintiff insurer holding that the family exclusion clause of an automobile insurance policy was effective to deny coverage for defendant husband in regard to the bodily injury liability claim of defendant wife, and thus plaintiff insurer did not have a duty to defend or indemnify defendant husband.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff insurer issued an automobile insurance liability policy to defendant husband in his name only covering a vehicle owned by him and defendant wife. Defendant wife was injured while she was riding as a passenger in the insured vehicle. Plaintiff insurer sued for declaratory relief to obtain a ruling on the family exclusion clause of the insurance policy issued to defendant husband. The lower court ruled that plaintiff did not have a duty to defend or indemnify defendant husband, and defendant wife appealed. Plaintiff's family member inclusion was authorized by Cal. Ins. Code § 11580.1(c). Defendant wife argued that Cal. Ins. Code § 11580.1 was in violation of the equal protection clauses of the state and federal constitutions to the extend that it permitted the exclusion. The arbitrary classification between family members and non-family members found in § 11580.1(c) was in contravention of well-established public policy of the state designed to limit exclusion from insurance coverage and to encourage coverage. The court found that § 11580.1(c)(5) and the family exclusion clause of the policy eliminated the rights of an entire class and exceeded rational bounds.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of plaintiff insurer because the court held that the statutory classification violated the equal protection guarantees of the state and federal constitution in that the disparate treatment accorded by the statute was not rationally related to a realistic legislative purpose.

 

1608 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ramirez


Crim. Nos. 34081, 34526, 36126


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


109 Cal. App. 3d 529; 167 Cal. Rptr. 174; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 2183



August 21, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Petition of Appellant Adam Salas Ramirez for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 15, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A341536, Carlos E. Velarde, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgments are affirmed. The petitions for writs of habeas corpus are denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants filed petitions for writs of habeas corpus seeking review of their convictions and sentences by the Superior Court, Los Angeles County (California) following a jury trial where appellants were found guilty of grand theft pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 487(1). The jury also found true the allegation that the loss exceeded $ 100,000 pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 12022.6(b). Appellants were sentenced to state prison.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, brothers, duped a bank into crediting one appellant's savings account with $ 1.5 million, based upon a fictitious wire transfer of funds. Appellants then withdrew $ 1.4 million from the account. One appellant was arrested at the airport boarding a plane to Ecuador. A jury found appellants guilty of grand theft pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 487(1) and found that the loss exceeded $ 100,000 pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 12022.6(b). Appellants were sentenced to prison. On appeal, the court affirmed appellants' convictions and their sentences. Appellants' contentions that Cal. Penal Code § 12022.6 was unconstitutionally vague, that the jury was inadequately instructed on its meaning, that the information gave appellants insufficient notice of the charge, and that appellants were precluded from arguing their interpretation to the jury, were based upon appellants' erroneous interpretation of the statute. The court rejected appellants' arguments regarding the pleading, instructions, and sufficiency of evidence of theft because none of the arguments had merit. The jury was properly instructed on flight, and any error that might have occurred was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court denied appellants' petitions for writs of habeas corpus. The court also affirmed appellants' convictions and sentences, finding that the evidence supported the two-year enhancement of their sentences, the jury was properly instructed on theft, and the evidence was sufficient to support appellants' convictions.

 

1609 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Hillerman


Civ. No. 16669


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


109 Cal. App. 3d 334; 167 Cal. Rptr. 240; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 2165



August 19, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Diego County, No. DN 14444, Richard D. Ring, Judge. *


* Pursuant to Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the interlocutory judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) in which the court refused to reserve jurisdiction for the purpose of dividing future Old Age, Survivors and Disability Insurance.


OVERVIEW: During appellee's and appellant's marriage, appellant had money deducted from his pay and deposited to Social Security. At the trial for dissolution of marriage, the court refused to reserve jurisdiction for the purpose of dividing future Old Age, Survivors and Disability Insurance (OASDI) on the basis that under California law, Social Security benefits were not community property. Upon review, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed because Congress intended to designate OASDI beneficiaries exclusive of any state domestic law.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the trial court was affirmed because Congress intended to designate Old Age, Survivors and Disability Insurance beneficiaries exclusive of any state domestic law.

 

1610 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Henderson


Crim. No. 35830


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


109 Cal. App. 3d 59; 167 Cal. Rptr. 47; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 2141



August 11, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 8, 1980. Mosk, J., Clark, J., and Newman, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A558522, Daniel L. Fletcher, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed as to count 4, the violation of section 12090. It is reversed as to count 1, but only insofar as it imposes a sentence for attempted robbery. In all other respects the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which found him guilty of attempted robbery, burglary, and other offenses including obliteration of identification of a handgun, on grounds that the trial court improperly instructed the jury on the presumption contained in Cal. Penal Code § 12091.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for several offenses arising out of an attempted robbery with the use of a firearm. He challenged his conviction for obliteration of the identification of a handgun in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 12091, on grounds that the trial court improperly instructed the jury on the presumption contained in the statute. Defendant contended that the instruction compelled the jury to find the presumed fact -- obliteration -- from the proved fact -- possession -- unless defendant himself came forward with evidence to rebut the presumption. The people denied that the instruction had any mandatory effect and claimed that it permitted the jury not to find the presumed fact even if no evidence on the identity of the obliterator other than the proved fact of possession was before it. On appeal, the court reversed the obliteration conviction, finding that the jury was improperly instructed that it must find obliteration if it finds possession, unless other evidence concerning the identity of the obliterator created a reasonable doubt that the culprit was defendant.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for obliteration of identification of a handgun was reversed because the jury was improperly instructed that the fact of his possession created a presumption that he had obliterated the handgun's identification absent evidence beyond a reasonable doubt that he was not the obliterator.

 

1611 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Bodenheimer v. Superior Court


Civ. No. 49003


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Four


108 Cal. App. 3d 885; 167 Cal. Rptr. 26; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 2121



August 4, 1980 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The alternative writ is discharged and the petition is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner organization member sought a writ commanding respondent Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) to refrain from compelling certain discovery, in the defamation action filed against petitioner and various associations, contending that the questions impinged upon his constitutional right of freedom of association.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner organization member sought a writ commanding respondent superior court to refrain from compelling certain discovery, in the defamation action filed against petitioner and various associations by real parties in interest, contending that the questions impinged upon his constitutional right of freedom of association. Petitioner was alleged to be an agent of one of the associations and working under its direction and supervision and with knowledge of its purposes. Asserting his U.S. Const. amend. I right to associational privacy, petitioner refused to answer in deposition whether he was a member of one of the defendant organizations, whether he knew any of the members, and whether he had participated in any of the meetings of the organization. The court denied the writ and held that to ask if petitioner was a member of that group was a narrow question having an important connection with the lawsuit. The court held that if the fact of membership was discoverable, the impact on privacy of the other two questions was too minimal to warrant extraordinary relief.


OUTCOME: Petitioner organization member's writ commanding respondent superior court to refrain from compelling discovery in the defamation action filed against petitioner and various associations by real parties in interest, was denied because the fact of membership was discoverable. The impact on privacy of the other questions as to whether petitioner knew the other members or participated in meetings was too minimal to warrant extraordinary relief.

 

1612 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Hernandez v. Department of Motor Vehicles


Civ. No. 58240


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA,SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


108 Cal. App. 3d 735; 166 Cal. Rptr. 694; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 2101



July 29, 1980 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Hg. granted Oct. 22, 1980 (See 30 C.3d 70)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No SWC 43611, George M. Dell, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied his petition for a writ of mandate to respondent Department of Motor Vehicles regarding a license suspension. Appellant sought to declare Cal. Veh. Code § 13353 unconstitutional. His license was suspended under § 13353 after he refused to submit to any chemical test when arrested for drunk driving under Cal. Veh. Code § 23102.


OVERVIEW: Appellant driver's license to operate a motor vehicle was suspended under Cal. Veh. Code § 13353, which provided for suspension on refusal to submit to any chemical test after an arrest for drunk driving. Drunk driving was a crime under Cal. Veh. Code § 23102. Appellant sought a writ of mandate from the trial court to respondent Department of Motor Vehicles and sought to declare § 13353 unconstitutional. The trial court denied the writ, and appellant sought review. The court affirmed the denial. The court held that the statutory scheme of § 13353 was constitutional. Under federal precedent, a state could summarily suspend a driver's license based on a refusal to submit to a chemical test. Statutes providing for license suspension such as § 13353, even without a suspension hearing, did not violate substantive or procedural due process. This was so even though a license to drive an automobile was an important interest similar to a property right. The court rejected appellant's argument that less drastic means were available to achieve the state's purpose. The court held that this was not the test and that the license suspension mechanism of § 13353 rationally served a valid purpose.


OUTCOME: Ruling in favor of respondent Department of Motor Vehicles, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment that denied appellant driver's petition for a writ of mandate. The court held that, as a matter of federal law from precedents, a state could summarily suspend a driver's license based upon a refusal of a chemical test. The court held further that the regulatory action of the statute in question was rationally related to a valid purpose.

 

1613 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Union Mutual Life Ins. Co. v. Kinder


Civ. No. 46126


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


108 Cal. App. 3d 517; 166 Cal. Rptr. 524; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 2077



July 24, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 729915, Ira A. Brown, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which granted respondent's motion for summary judgment in appellant's action seeking to declare that Cal. Ins. Code § 10127.15, which invalidated "nonfreeze" insurance policy provisions, applied prospectively only.


OVERVIEW: Prior to a state law prohibiting the sale of "nonfreeze" policies, respondent insurance agency sold "nonfreeze" long-term disability insurance, which reduced the amount of benefits proportionate to certain other income an insured received. Appellant, the state's insurance commissioner, argued that an amendment to the statute invalidated the application of "nonfreeze" provisions to insured individuals who were disabled prior to the statute's effective date, as well as insured individuals not disabled by the effective date of the underlying statute. Analyzing the amendment's legislative history, the court held it did not apply retroactively to individuals insured under nonfreeze policies that were disabled prior to the statute's effective date, as the legislature had rejected a provision that would have explicitly made the statute retroactive. Thus, the court held the statute's amendment applied only to "nonfreeze" policy holders not disabled at the time the statute came into effect.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, as the statutory amendment did not apply retroactively.

 

1614 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Kaylor v. Superior Court


Civ. No. 18905


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


108 Cal. App. 3d 451; 166 Cal. Rptr. 598; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 2070



July 22, 1980 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Let a peremptory writ issue ordering the superior court to suppress the evidence found in the two residences we have found were unconstitutionally searched.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought a writ ordering respondent trial court to suppress certain evidence seized from his home pursuant to a search warrant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a motion seeking to suppress evidence obtained from the search of his home. Defendant asserted that the search warrant failed because the affidavits were largely illegible and could not be the basis for probable cause. Respondent trial court denied defendant's motion. Defendant sought a writ seeking the suppression of the evidence. The court granted defendant's writ. According to the court, the protection afforded by U.S. Const. amend. IV consisted of requiring that the inferences that a crime was committed be drawn by a neutral and detached magistrate instead of being judged by the officer engaged in the often competitive enterprise of ferreting out crime. The court held that the magistrate must judge for himself the persuasiveness of the facts relied on by a complaining officer to show probable cause. The court found that the search warrant was deficient because portions of the supporting affidavit incorporated were illegible, and because the magistrate did not read some of the reports which formed a part of the affidavit. The court concluded that the portions that were not read could not form the basis for probable cause.


OUTCOME: The appeals court granted defendant's writ ordering that certain evidence seized from his home be suppressed because portions of the supporting affidavit were illegible and because the magistrate did not read some of the reports which formed a part of the affidavit.

 

1615 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Clingenpeel v. Municipal Court


Civ. Nos. 56984, 57591, 57590


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


108 Cal. App. 3d 394; 166 Cal. Rptr. 573; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 2063



July 21, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied September 17, 1980. Manuel, J., was of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Nos. C 258429, C 258428, and C 258427, Jerry Pacht, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state, as a real party in interest, disputed the grants by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), of three writs of prohibition directed to respondent Municipal Court for the Antelope Judicial District of Los Angeles County. The issue was whether charging defendants with drunken bicycle riding violated their constitutional right to procedural due process.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged, under Cal. Veh. Code § 23102, with drunken bicycle riding. Respondent municipal court denied defendants' demurrers. The appellate court issued writs of prohibition to respondent, and the state, as a real party in interest, appealed. The court held that, under Cal. Veh. Code § 670, a bicycle was excluded from Cal. Veh. Code § 23102. The court reviewed the legislative history of Cal. Veh. Code § 21200, which real party in interest argued did support the charges against defendants. The court held that a 1943 amendment to its predecessor statute, Cal. Veh. Code § 452, had rendered that statute ambiguous. The ambiguity was continued, and perhaps made worse, in § 21200. Under § 21200, routine traffic infractions did not subject cyclists to criminal punishment. It was therefore unlikely that the legislature intended to make severe drunk driving penalties applicable to defendants. Because § 21200 did not explicitly inform defendants that drunken bicycle riding would subject them to criminal punishment, to so apply it to them would violate their constitutional right to procedural due process. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the writs of prohibition. The court held that, under the relevant statute, a bicycle was not a "vehicle." The version of the statute sought to be applied to defendants was ambiguous. Because the statute did not explicitly inform them that drunken bicycle riding would subject them to criminal punishment, to so apply it to them would violate their constitutional right to procedural due process.

 

1616 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Martin


Crim. No. 34727


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


107 Cal. App. 3d 714; 165 Cal. Rptr. 773; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 1992



June 27, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A-435397, Peter H. Stevens, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that extended his commitment as a mentally disordered sex offender pursuant to the Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6316.2.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with kidnapping, in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 207, lewd conduct on a child under the age of 14, in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 288, and forcible oral copulation on a child under the age of 14, in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 288a. Appellant pled guilty as charged to lewd conduct and the other two charges were dismissed. Defendant was committed to confinement in a state hospital after he was found to be a mentally disordered sex offender (MDSO) pursuant to the Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6316.2. After a hearing to determine whether appellant should be released, his term of commitment was extended. Appellant sought review. The court found that it would be cruel and unusual punishment if appellant was recommitted as a MDSO when he could not benefit from such treatment. The court applied the substantial evidence rule to determine whether appellant was amenable to treatment and found that there was sufficient evidence for a reasonable trier of fact to believe beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant could benefit from additional treatment. The prosecutor was not required to show appellant would be cured, only that appellant would benefit from treatment.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the lower court that extended appellant's commitment to a hospital after appellant was found to be a mentally disordered sex offender was affirmed because the prosecutor was only required to appellant would benefit from the confinement, and there was expert testimony that appellant would benefit by continued confinement.

California Computer Products, Inc. v. County of Orange


Civ. No. 21536


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


107 Cal. App. 3d 731; 166 Cal. Rptr. 68; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 1994



June 27, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied September 3, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. 282657, Alicemarie H. Stotler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of an order of the Superior Court, Orange County (California) granting defendant county's motion for summary judgment in plaintiff's action for partial refund of taxes on its business inventories, which were assessed on the tax roll as escaped property.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff taxpayer filed business property statements with defendant county for each of the fiscal years 1972-1974. Defendant audited plaintiff's books and disclosed that plaintiff failed to reflect accurately the costs of the business inventories, and entered escaped business inventory assessments for those years. Plaintiff appealed to an assessment appeals board, which reduced the assessed value but declined to rule on the exemption claim. Plaintiff paid the taxes under protest and brought an action against defendant. The trial court granted defendant's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed the motion for summary judgment, ruling that defendant's right to recover taxes on business inventories escaping assessment accrued on the lien date of the fiscal year in which the escape occurred, and not on the date of entry on the tax roll.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the motion for summary judgment ruling that defendant county's right to recover taxes on plaintiff taxpayer's business inventories escaping assessment accrued on the lien date of the fiscal year in which the escape occurred, and not on the date of entry on the tax roll.

 

1618 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Poggi


Crim. No. 34250


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


107 Cal. App. 3d 581; 165 Cal. Rptr. 758; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 1986



June 26, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied August 28, 1980. Tobriner, J., and Newman, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A 431512, Harry V. Peetris, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order of commitment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court, Los Angeles County (California), in a criminal action, where the trial court had extended appellant's commitment to the Department of Mental Health, as a mentally disordered sex offender, for one year pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6316.2.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's commitment to the Department of Mental Health as a mentally disordered sex offender was extended for one year, pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6316.2. He challenged the trial court's order, contending that the extended commitment should be reversed in the absence of a finding that appellant was amenable to treatment. The court affirmed. Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6316.1 provided that the appellant could not have been kept in actual custody longer than the maximum term of prison commitment for the original offense, except as provided in § 6316.2. Section 6316.2 provided that a person may be committed beyond the term prescribed by Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code 6316.1. Sections 6316.1 and 6316.2 were added by 1977 Cal. Stat. 164 in order to provide additional safeguards against the premature release of dangerous persons. Appellant met all the requirements of § 6316.2. His "sex offense" was a felony, he suffered from a mental disorder, and as a result of such mental disorder, was predisposed to the commission of sexual offenses to such a degree that he presented a serious threat of substantial harm to the health and safety of others.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court extending for one year appellant's commitment to the Department of Mental Health, as a mentally disordered sex offender, because appellant met all the statutory requirements for extension.

 

1619 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Henderson


Crim. No. 9939


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


107 Cal. App. 3d 475; 166 Cal. Rptr. 20; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 1980



June 25, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied August 28, 1980. Mosk, J., and Newman, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, No. 47822, William H. Lally, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which extended for one year under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6316.2 appellant's commitment to a state hospital as a medically disordered sex offender.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued trial court error in extending, pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6316.2, his commitment to a state hospital as a medically disordered sex offender (MDSO) following his plea of guilty to felony charges involving a minor. The court disagreed, ruling that expert testimony of mental health professionals finding appellant to constitute a serious threat of harm to others was admissible, as admissibility was not so much based on the predictability of uncertain future violent behavior as on appellant's present predisposition to committing violence. Moreover, appellant's ex post facto challenge to the constitutionality of § 6316.2 was without merit, as appellant did not have a vested right in the ameliorative provisions of the determinate sentencing law prior to its operative, as opposed to effective, date. And as appellant fell within a class of offenders shown to pose a danger to others, he was properly subject to extended commitment without violating equal protection laws. Finally, the court rejected the contention that § 6316.2 was vague or that, to be constitutional, its standards for commitment release must equate with the requirements for commitment.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed extending for one year appellant's commitment to a state hospital as a medically disordered sex offender, because extension statute was not constitutionally defective as ex post facto law or violative of appellant's equal protection and due process rights, and because expert testimony of mental health professionals was properly admissible to show appellant's predisposition toward violence that posed threat of harm to others.

 

1620 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wright


Crim. No. 4076.


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


107 Cal. App. 3d 372; 165 Cal. Rptr. 631; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 1972



June 24, 1980 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Hg. granted Oct. 15, 1980 (See 30 C.3d 705)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Kern County, No. 19616, William A. Stone, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Kern County (California) that convicted him of two counts of burglary based upon guilty pleas. Appellant challenged his sentences, claiming Cal. Penal Code § 1170.3 was unconstitutional, the trial court erred in applying mitigating and aggravating factors, aggravation by prior conviction was double jeopardy, and counsel was ineffective.


OVERVIEW:  Cal. Penal Code § 1170.3 and the sentencing rules promulgated thereunder were constitutional. It was not improper for the legislature to authorize the judiciary to establish sentencing guidelines, as sentencing was an inherently judicial function. Based on all the aggravating and mitigating factors, imposition of the upper term was not improper. Assuming that the trial court erred in counting as multiple victims under Cal. R. Ct. 421(a)(4), the victims of two distinct offenses for which appellant was convicted, there still remained to be considered the great monetary value of the property stolen under Cal. R. Ct. 421(a)(10), and appellant's nine prior convictions in 11 years. Appellant did not prove the mitigating factor of necessity, Cal. R. Ct. 423(a)(8). His plea was not tainted by the omission of an asserted condition of his plea bargain conference, as he did not ask to withdraw his plea when it was omitted. A victim's inflammatory remark did not influence the sentencing decision, enhancement by prior conviction was not double jeopardy, and appellant failed to prove any deficiency in counsel's performance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions and sentences. The court held that the sentencing rules were constitutional. The trial court, on balance, correctly applied the aggravating and mitigating factors to the case. Appellant had not been subjected to double jeopardy, and his counsel did not render ineffective assistance.

 

1621 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Dunn


Crim. No. 18148


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


107 Cal. App. 3d 138; 165 Cal. Rptr. 574; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 1948



June 19, 1980 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As modified June 30, 1980.
Hg. den. Aug. 28, 1980, and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.).


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Alameda County, No. 65286, Alan A. Lindsay, Winton McKibben and Martin N. Pulich, Judges.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his Superior Court of Alameda County (California) conviction for having had sexual intercourse with two women under 18 in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 261.5.


OVERVIEW: Officers stopped two young girls on a hunch that the girls were prostitutes. Upon investigation, the underaged girls admitted to having had sexual intercourse with appellant. The girls' confessions were used to convict appellant of having sexual intercourse with two women under 18 in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 261.5. The court of appeals reversed. The investigatory stop of the two girls could not be justified. They were stopped because the officers believed they were prostitutes, yet the officers did not claim, nor could they claim, that the girls were soliciting customers. The only "conduct" alleged was the fact that the girls were young, dressed provocatively, and in an area in which prostitution activity was centered. These did not constitute specific and articulable facts rendering the officers' suspicion objectively reasonable. Evidence obtained as a result of the girls' unlawful detention could not be admitted against appellant.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for having had sexual intercourse with two women under 18 was reversed because the evidence used to convict appellant was the result of an illegal detention.

 

1622 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Barry v. City of Oceanside


Civ. No. 22322


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


107 Cal. App. 3d 257; 165 Cal. Rptr. 697; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 1963



June 19, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Diego County, No. N 11747, Michael L. Burley, Temporary Judge. *


* Pursuant to Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed with directions to issue a peremptory writ of mandate as prayed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, bookstore owners, appealed the judgment from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) that denied their petition for a writ of mandate challenging the revocation of the license to their adult bookstore by respondent, a city, pursuant to City of Oceanside, Cal., City Code § 15.3(18). Petitioners claimed that § 15.3(18) was vague, overbroad, and violated petitioners' U.S. Const. amend, I rights of free speech.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, bookstore owners, had arcade booths for peepshows in their adult bookstore. Because customers at the peepshow were arrested and convicted for causing a public nuisance by masturbating while in the booths, respondent, a city, revoked petitioners' business license under Oceanside, Cal., City Code § 15.3(18) for operating a business in a manner that threatened the public health, welfare, or safety. The trial court denied their petition for a writ of mandate challenging the revocation. On appeal, the court held that because § 15.3(18) impinged on petitioners' U.S. Const. amend. I rights of free speech and press, the ordinance was subject to strict scrutiny. Because § 15.3(18) gave broad discretion to public officials to determine what constituted harm to the public health, welfare or safety without giving clear standards that were susceptible to objective measurement as to what constituted the harm, § 15.3(18) was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. Therefore, the court reversed the order with directions to issue a peremptory writ of mandate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying the petition of petitioners, bookstore owners, for a writ of mandate challenging the revocation of the license for their adult bookstore for causing a public harm and ordered the writ to be issued. The court held that because the ordinance did not provide objective standards on what constituted a harm, it impermissibly infringed on petitioners' constitutional rights of free speech and press.

 

1623 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Hewitt v. Rincon del Diablo Municipal Water Dist.


Civ. No. 18677


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


107 Cal. App. 3d 78; 165 Cal. Rptr. 545; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 1943



June 18, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The petition of plaintiffs and respondents for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied August 13, 1980. The United States Supreme Court denied a petition for writ of certiorari on January 12, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. N 8616, Wesley B. Buttermore, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city sought review of an order of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) that found a merger agreement was not valid and prevented construction of flumes necessary to interconnect two water systems.


OVERVIEW: Defendant water district was a public agency. Defendant city's land partially was included within defendant water district's boundaries. Defendants entered a merger agreement to fully merge their water systems. Plaintiff landowners filed suit to prevent construction of flumes necessary to interconnect the project. The trial court found the merger was not valid. Defendant city appealed. Municipal water districts were characterized as quasi-municipal corporations and had a broad grant of legislative policy-making power. The court found the merger agreement was a contract of cooperation by two public agencies who joined together to form one integrated water system. The merger agreement was not fatally defective merely because it did not specify a time for its termination. The court reversed because the merger agreement did not substitute defendant city's council for defendant water district's board of directors. The court found the legislative purpose of Cal. Water Code § 71699 was to preserve financial integrity and to insure repayment of indebtedness incurred to provide water service, and that purpose was accomplished by the merger.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the lower court that found a merger agreement between defendant city and defendant water district was invalid was reversed because defendant water district was characterized as quasi-municipal corporation and had a broad grant of legislative policy-making power. The merger agreement did not substitute defendant city's council for defendant water district's board of directors.

 

1624 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Peace


Crim. No. 19276


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


107 Cal. App. 3d 996; 166 Cal. Rptr. 202; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 2022



June 16, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied July 11, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 98262, William E. Mullins, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed. Appellant's work time/good time credit can be computed after retrial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) that convicted him and found true a sentence enhancement under Cal. Penal Code § 1203.09. Appellant claimed the trial court disregarded his mental illness, failed to state reasons for enhancing his sentence, § 1203.09 was unconstitutional, his waiver of a jury trial was invalid; and he was entitled to work or good time credit.


OVERVIEW: The trial court did not abuse its discretion in failing to send appellant to a diagnostic facility pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 1203.03. There was ample evidence of appellant's instability, but the court assumed, consistent with Cal. Evid. Code § 664, that the trial court properly considered the evidence before rejecting it. The sentence enhancement for a prior conviction under Cal. Penal Code § 667.5(b) was compulsory. It was not necessary for the trial court to state reasons, pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 1170(c), for not striking a compulsory sentence. The court held that there was no scienter element for Cal. Penal Code § 1203.09 because it was not a criminal offense. Section 1203.09 did not violate equal protection because it was classified by victim, not perpetrator. All this was for naught, however, because as defense counsel had voiced disapproval of appellant's waiver of jury, the waiver was invalid under Cal. Const. art. I, § 16. There was no constitutional right to waive jury over counsel's objection. The trial court also erred in not granting sentence credit as required by Cal. Penal Code § 4019(b), (c).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded for a new trial. The trial court erred in accepting appellant's waiver of jury in the face of counsel's disapproval of the waiver. Appellant's other contentions regarding the illegality or inappropriateness of his sentence, aside from the lack of credit for presentence custody, were without merit.

Foundation for San Francisco's Architectural Heritage v. City and County of San Francisco


Civ. No. 48599


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


106 Cal. App. 3d 893; 165 Cal. Rptr. 401; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 1924



June 12, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied July 11, 1980, and appellants' petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied August 21, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 749536, Ira A. Brown, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant architectural society sought review of an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which denied appellant's petition for a writ of administrative mandamus seeking to vacate respondent city's issuance of a permit allowing for the demolition of a historic landmark building.


OVERVIEW: The board of permit appeals of respondent city approved permits for the demolition of a historic landmark building and the construction of a new department store in its place. Appellant architectural society filed a petition in the trial court for a writ of administrative mandamus to vacate the permits on the basis that the building was a historic landmark. The trial court denied the writ. The court affirmed, holding that respondent complied with the substantive and procedural requirements of the California Environmental Quality Act. There was no evidence that respondent's environmental impact statement (EIR) on the proposed demolition was impartial or that respondent unlawfully delegated its review functions to the project developer. The EIR described in good faith the reasonable alternatives to demolition, and respondent's findings were sufficiently detailed so as to comply with Cal. Pub. Res. Code § 21081. The California historic preservation statutes did not prohibit demolition, and the city's master plan did not mandate the building's historic preservation. Respondent properly exercised its discretion in balancing the elements of the city's master plan.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of appellant architectural society's petition for a writ of administrative mandamus seeking to vacate a demolition permit for a historic landmark building because respondent properly exercised its discretion in balancing the elements of the city's master plan and complied with the applicable environmental and state historic preservation statutes.

 

1626 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Cotton v. Superior Court of Los Angeles County


Civ. No. 58294


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA,SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


106 Cal. App. 3d 833; 165 Cal. Rptr. 374; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 1920



June 11, 1980 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Deleted on direction of Supreme Court by order dated August 8, 1980.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant petitioned for a writ of mandate to direct the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) to vacate its order denying his motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped by a police officer based on his license plate's similarity to one seen near a robbery-homicide. He was handcuffed, but was told he was not under arrest. Officers involved with the case arrived and questioned him without advising him of his Miranda rights. When he said he had been near the scene and had purchased a soda of a brand found at the scene, he was arrested. Defendant's motion to suppress evidence was denied by the trial court. The court directed that defendant's motion be granted. The officer who stopped defendant acknowledged she knew nothing about the case sufficient for her to arrest or detain petitioner, but did so upon direction of another officer. That officer admitted he did not have sufficient information to believe defendant was involved in the robbery. This was an arrest because defendant was handcuffed and not free to leave. Even if it was not, the arrest by the second officer was without probable cause. Other than the inference that petitioner was in the area of the robbery-homicide at about the time it occurred, the only evidence known to the officer was that a certain brand of soda pop can was found at the robbery site.


OUTCOME: The court directed the lower court to vacate its order denying defendant's motion to suppress evidence and to enter a new order granting defendant's motion. The first officer to encounter defendant knew nothing about the case, and the officer at whose direction she detained defendant did not have sufficient information to believe defendant was involved in the robbery. Defendant was thus arrested without probable cause.

Lackner v. St. Joseph Convalescent Hospital, Inc.


Civ. No. 44772


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Four


106 Cal. App. 3d 542; 165 Cal. Rptr. 198; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 1898



June 5, 1980 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Alameda County, No. 490803-6, Robert L. Bostick, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital sought review of judgment from the Superior Court of Alameda County, (California) that upheld respondent health department director's affirmance of an administrative hearing citation under the Long-Term Care, Health, Safety, and Security Act of 1973 (Act), Cal. Health & Safety Code §§ 1417- 1429, and granted summary judgment for respondent on appellant's cross-complaint, which challenged the constitutionality of the Act.


OVERVIEW: Appellant hospital sought review of the trial court judgment that upheld respondent health department director's affirmance of an administrative citation issued for violations of patient care under the Long-Term Care, Health, Safety, and Security Act of 1973 (Act), Cal. Health & Safety Code §§ 1417- 1429 and granted summary judgment against appellant on its cross-complaint challenging the constitutionality of the Act. The court affirmed the trial court judgment that found that the inadequate patient care provided by appellant constituted a class "A" violation pursuant to Cal. Health and Safety § 1424(a). The court rejected appellant's argument that the Act was unconstitutionally vague. The court found that the Act, which defined violations as those that "present an imminent danger" or "substantial probability" of death or "serious physical harm" was sufficiently definite to provide notice as to acts forbidden. The court rejected the equal protection challenge, explaining the statutory classifications for long term and acute care facilities met the rational relationship test because of substantial difference as to staff member qualifications in the institution types.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment holding that the Long-Term Care, Health, Safety, and Security Act of 1973 (Act) was not unconstitutional because its terms were reasonably certain by reference to definable regulations and its classifications were rationally related to differing qualifications and requirements for facility type and that evidence established that inadequate patient care provided by appellant was a statutory violation.

Lee v. Davis


Civ. No. 56433; Civ. No. 56620; Civ. No. 56750; Civ. No. 56754


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA,SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, law enforcement officers, appealed from a decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that granted preliminary injunctions restricting them from enforcing, prior to another trial on the merits, ordinances of the city regulating establishments that provided nude or seminude dancing in establishments serving food and drink.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought action against defendants, law enforcement officers, seeking a preliminary injunction restricting defendants from enforcing, prior to another trial on the merits, ordinances of the city regulating establishments that provide nude or seminude dancing in establishments serving food and drink. The court found that plaintiffs would likely succeed in proving its case challenging the ordinance.

 

1629 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


People v. Haynes


Crim. No. 34987


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA,SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


106 Cal. App. 3d 413; 165 Cal. Rptr. 138; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 1886



June 2, 1980 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Hg. den. July 30, 1980, and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art VI, § 14  [**1] rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A078447, Edward Rafeedie, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant challenged the ruling of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Super. Ct. No. A078447 (California), which convicted him of robbery and enhanced his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendant appealed from his conviction for violation of Cal. Penal Code § 211. Defendant pleaded guilty to that offense following denial of his motion to suppress evidence. He was sentenced to five years in the state prison, plus one year enhancement for a prior felony conviction. On appeal, defendant challenged the propriety of the trial court's ruling on his motion to suppress evidence, asserting that the officers had no probable cause to search the trunk of his car. In this case, the officer believed that defendant had recently had contraband in his possession. Under these circumstances, it was reasonable to assume that it had been secreted in the trunk of the car, and probable cause to search there existed. Therefore, the constitutional rights of defendant were not violated. Also, the court noted that defendant's reimprisonment for a parole violation was included as part of the initial imprisonment and was not deemed a separate second felony offense. Therefore, defendant's sentence was properly enhanced for a period of one year.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling of the trial court which convicted defendant of robbery and enhanced his sentence by one year where it was shown that the officers had probable cause to search defendant's car trunk. Therefore, defendant's constitutional rights were not violated. Also, the enhanced sentence was proper due to defendant's prior felony conviction.

People v. E.W.A.P., Inc.


Civ. No. 55992


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Five


106 Cal. App. 3d 315; 165 Cal. Rptr. 73; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 1878



May 29, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondents' petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied August 21, 1980. Tobriner, J., Mosk, J., and Newman, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C 236269, Robert I. Weil, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order of dismissal is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the People of California, appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which dismissed plaintiff's complaint. Plaintiff had sought to enjoin defendant corporation and its officers from commercially distributing copies of obscene films and magazines in violation of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 17200.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, the People of California, filed complaint to enjoin defendant corporation and its officers from commercially distributing copies of obscene films and magazines. Plaintiff alleged that such distribution was an unlawful business practice as defined under Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 17200. The trial court sustained defendants' demurrer and dismissed plaintiff's complaint. The court reversed the order of dismissal. The court agreed with plaintiff that the complaint adequately alleged an unlawful business practice within the meaning of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 17200. The court held that trafficking in obscene matter, an illegal practice under Cal. Penal Code § 311.2, came within Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 17200 when it was practiced as a business. The court held that plaintiff did not have to allege additionally that defendant's activities were anticompetitive or harmful to the consumer of such products. The court held that the possible application of civil penalties did not render statute unconstitutional, rejecting defendants' argument that civil penalties would amount to a penal sanction in violation of due process of law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of dismissal, holding that the complaint adequately alleged that defendants' commercial distribution of obscene matter was an unlawful business practice within the meaning of the applicable California statute.

Neogard Corp. v. Malott & Peterson-Grundy


Civ. No. 44406


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


106 Cal. App. 3d 213; 164 Cal. Rptr. 813; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 1868



May 28, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied June 27, 1980, and appellant's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied July 23, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, Nos. 675658, 676022, S. Lee Vavuris, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant foreign corporation challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) which found it lacked capacity to maintain an action based on intrastate commerce under Cal. Corp. Code §§ 2105, 2203 (c), asserting that it engaged only in interstate commerce.


OVERVIEW: Appellant foreign corporation filed an action to recover the costs to repair waterproofing projects which appellee contractor completed using appellant's product. Appellee raised the affirmative defense of appellant's incapacity because it had not obtained a qualifying certificate under Cal. Corp. Code § 2105. The trial court found appellant was engaged in intrastate business and dismissed the action under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 2203 (c). Appellant sought review, asserting that it was engaged in interstate business and that the action involved an interstate contract. The court affirmed. It ruled that appellant's in-state activities, which included sending sales representatives, entering contracts, and supervising its product's use, taken together, constituted intrastate business and that, thus, appellant was compelled to qualify to conduct such business under § 2105. The action involved intrastate activities and was properly dismissed under § 2203(c).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment entered for appellee contractor because appellant foreign corporation was engaged in intrastate business and was required to obtain a certificate to qualify to do business in the state. Having failed to do so, appellant lacked the capacity to maintain an action based on intrastate business.

 

1632 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


In re Gregory K.


Civ. No. 56903


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


106 Cal. App. 3d 164; 165 Cal. Rptr. 35; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 1864



May 27, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied July 23, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. J 814626, Harry J. Kightlinger, Temporary Judge * Referee.


* Pursuant to Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: The order of the juvenile court directing Susan K. to pay $ 645.24 to the county is vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother of juvenile offender sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) which ordered appellant to pay the costs of maintaining appellant's child in a county detention center pursuant to a petition which was subsequently dismissed for lack of sufficient evidence.


OVERVIEW: Minor sentenced and detained as a juvenile. Juvenile court found that evidence contained involuntary statements of the minor; therefore, juvenile court dismissed petition and ordered the minor released. Respondent County of Los Angeles sent a request for payment from appellant mother for the period of the minor's confinement, which appellant refused to pay. The court vacated the order of the juvenile court that ordered appellant to pay respondent the requested amount. The court found that the trial court could not impose liability on a minor's parents for confinement where the evidence was insufficient to establish that the minor committed a crime, which was the only basis for wardship. The court found that the parental duty of support was not a basis to requiring appellant to reimburse respondent for the cost of maintaining the minor in involuntary custody.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order of the juvenile court directing appellant mother to pay for her child's confinement, because juvenile court dismissed petition against minor and ordered him released from custody. The court found that, under these circumstances, the parental duty of support was not a basis for requiring appellant to reimburse respondent for the cost of maintaining the minor in involuntary custody.

Stone v. State of California


Civ. No. 18317


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


106 Cal. App. 3d 924; 165 Cal. Rptr. 339; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 1926



May 23, 1980 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified May 28, 1980. A petition for a rehearing was denied June 16, 1980, and appellants' petition for a hearing by the Supreme Court was denied July 30, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, Nos. 261681, 262681, Richard E. Tuttle, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured persons appealed an order by the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California) which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant public entity in plaintiffs' claim for injuries suffered while on defendant's property as a result of an alleged failure by defendant to provide adequate security.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff injured persons filed a claim in tort against defendant public entity for injuries plaintiffs suffered while on defendant's property. Plaintiffs based liability upon the theory that their injuries were caused by a dangerous condition of defendant's property, a statutory basis for public liability under Cal. Gov't Code § 835. Plaintiffs were on defendant's property when they were attacked and injured. Plaintiffs alleged that defendants failed to provide adequate security on its property. Defendants filed a motion for summary judgment, which was granted by the lower court. Plaintiffs appealed, and the court affirmed summary judgment. The court held that defendant's liability as a public entity rested upon statute and was subject to statutory immunities. The court held that plaintiffs' claims rested exclusively upon a failure to provide sufficient police protection and that this failure was specifically immunized from liability by Cal. Gov't Code § 845. The court concluded that on the strength of prior caselaw, § 845 was constitutional and did not deny plaintiffs equal protection of laws.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of defendant public entity and against plaintiff injured persons. The court held that plaintiffs' claims rested exclusively upon a failure to provide sufficient police protection. The court held that this failure was specifically immunized from liability by statute.

 

1634 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Mackey v. Panish


Civ. Nos. 59097, 59136


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


106 Cal. App. 3d 7; 164 Cal. Rptr. 771; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 1853



May 22, 1980 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The petitions are denied.

The parties to bear their own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner candidate and respondent registrar-recorders were before the court (California) on two petitions for writ of mandate. Petitioner sought to have a prepayment requirement for accepting candidate's statements, authorized by Cal. Elec. Code § 10012, declared unconstitutional, and to enforce an order by the state supreme court that respondents refrain from enforcing the prepayment requirement while the instant matter was pending.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner candidate filed two petitions for writ of mandate against respondent registrar-recorders. By the first petition he sought a determination that a prepayment requirement in Cal. Elec. Code § 10012 for accepting candidate statements was unconstitutional. By the second petition, he sought compliance with a state supreme court order directing respondents to refrain from implementing the prepayment requirement while the instant matter was being resolved. The court denied both petitions. The court held that the statute met constitutional requirements, and that respondents were not compelled to subsidize or extend credit to petitioner, who was a non-indigent, for what was essentially a campaign expense. In considering the second petition, equity required the court to balance respondents' conduct against that of petitioner. The court held that while respondents may have been in contempt, petitioner was partly to blame for waiting so long to submit his report. The court held that forcing respondents to comply with the order would substantially disrupt the election process and it would be unfair to those candidates who had paid their share of the costs.


OUTCOME: The court denied both petitions for writ of mandate. The court held that respondent registrar-recorders were not compelled to subsidize the campaign costs of petitioner candidate, who was a non-indigent. The court held that to enforce the state supreme court order at that time would substantially disrupt the election process.

 

1635 of 2274 DOCUMENTS


Messina v. Workers' Comp. Appeals Bd.


Civ. No. 56194


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


105 Cal. App. 3d 964; 164 Cal. Rptr. 762; 1980 Cal. App. LEXIS 1844; 45 Cal. Comp. Cases 505



May 21, 1980 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The decision of the board is annulled and the matter remanded to the board for such further proceedings as are consistent with our opinion herein.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner husband appealed the decision of the California Workers' Compensation Appeals Board which awarded death benefits to his dependent children based on plaintiff's wife's employment-related injury that resulted in her death, but denied augmented death benefits under Cal. Lab. Code § 4702 for dependent children and widows.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner's wife died of an injury arising out of and occurring in the course of her employment. The couple had two minor children. The California Workers' Compensation Appeals Board awarded the children a death benefit of $ 40,000. The children claimed entitlement to the augmented death benefit of $ 45,000, which was awarded to "a surviving widow and one or more dependent minor children" under Cal. Lab. Code § 4702. On appeal, the court determined that the limitation of augmented death benefits to widows was unconstitutional under the equal protection clauses of both the United States and California Constitutions and held that § 4702 had to be read to also provide the augmented death benefit to a surviving widower and one or more dependent minor children. The decision of the board was annulled.


OUTCOME: The court annulled the California Workers' Compensation Appeals Board's decision which denied augmented death benefits, and the court remanded the case to the board because the limitation of augmented death benefits to widows was unconstitutional under the equal protection clauses of both the United States and California Constitutions, and the provision had to be read to include widowers.
